< text>
It's a nice park but 4 or a 5 stars?, No Way ! The park, like so many of the older parks in Camarillo, has NO RESTROOM FACILITIES. So you can't stay for long (if you know what I mean !). But I guess if you don't eat or drink anything while you're there you'll be ok. Put in a Port-a-potty and I'll give it a 3.<//text>

< review>
Best pizza I've had in Los Angeles, CA, hands down. Both deep dish and thin crust options. <Text>This place is very impressed with itself, while I am not quite as impressed.

Walked up to the door and the vibe immediately started with the valet guy..."do you have a reservation?" *sigh* Yes, we have a reservation. The website, reviews, everywhere says Reservations Only. No Pictures blah blah blah. I get it.

Smaller place than I expected. We were promptly seated at our table for a 7:30 reservation, which was nice. Except our table was so close to the 4 top next to us that we felt like we were at their table with them, in their laps, which was not so nice. And they were soooooo loud that I could not hear my dining companion. First of all, they should have some manners and tone it down a bit now that someone is next to them. Second of all, the restaurant should have asked them to take it down a notch, especially after I mentioned to the waiter that they were realllllly loud and we couldn't hear each other for our own conversation. Thank god they left about 15 min into our dinner and the place resumed to a normal decibel level.

For food we ordered the following to share:
Calamari - very salty
Margherita pizza - nothing to write home about
Corn & Lobster Mezzaluna - good, about 6 raviolis
Roasted Cauliflower - this was delicious, surprisingly my favorite dish
Chocolate Budino - small pot of a very rich chocolate

Service was ok...it took us forever to get our drinks. I think we had the calamari and pizza before the drinks even came. Each dish came out as it was ready. Would have been nice to have the pasta and cauliflower together.

All in all, if was an A-OK dining experience, but nothing to ooooh and aaaaah over.

Would I come back? Naw, I'll pass. I prefer Craig's.

Bonus: Ambiance
Bogus: trying too hard to be the "it" Hollywood place.</Text>< username>

<Text>How was the food? Don‚Äôt know. Service? Not a clue. Decor and ambiance? Looked great for a fleeting moment as the affectless hostess escorted us through the well-appointed dining room and into what looked like a back alley on a cold February night. We and another couple made a reservation and secured babysitters weeks before our February 23 first visit to The Nice Guy. A few days before, the restaurant called to say they needed to move us from 7:30 to 8:00. Weird, but fine. My wife and I arrived a few minutes before 8:00 and before our friends so we went to the bar. The place looked beautiful and we were excited to have a meal there. Our friends arrived a few minutes later. But then the hostess escorted us away from the elegant and enticing dining room and out a side door into what I would describe as a side alley where 3 tables had been set, seemingly as an afterthought. We were the only ones in the alley. It was cold. No ambiance. No lighting. No candles on the tables. No flowers. Just an alley with 3 tables. The expressionless, unapologetic hostess said she would turn on the outdoor heaters. 2 out of 3 of them didn‚Äôt work. We asked if we could wait at the bar for a table inside. The unsmiling hostess said yes, and that a table ‚Äúmight‚Äù become available ‚Äúaround 10:30‚Äù (it was 8:05 and the babysitter clock was ticking). She didn‚Äôt seem to appreciate the absurdity of us waiting at the bar for two-and-a-half hours for the chance‚Äîmaybe a slim chance?‚Äîat an indoor table. Unhappy with the cold, dark, cramped outdoor seating, and with fluorescent lighting from the street shining in our faces, we asked to see a manager. When no manager appeared for 10 minutes, we booked AOC on OpenTable for 8:30 and left. The manager appeared outside as the valet retrieved our cars. He was very apologetic and invited us back another night. He seemed nice but it was too late. LA has so many great restaurants to try and we don‚Äôt have enough bandwidth (or babysitters) to try them all. By the way, AOC was terrific (as always)‚Äîthe hostess even smiled, made a joke and seemed really happy to have us, which was a different and refreshing experience that evening. I‚Äôve probably eaten out a couple of thousand times in my adult life and never have been treated like this. Life is short. Babysitters cost money. <rating>4<//rating>< text>
So I hadn't anticipated on loving this restaurant from previous reviews I had read.  I expected snobby, pretentious, too cool for you kind of restaurant.  When I read that you are not allowed even inside the restaurant without a reservation, that you have a specific time limit to eat and about bad service, I walked in already with thoughts of what I was going to put on my review.

My friend and I were about 10 minutes late for a reservation, no problem, walked us right in and to our seat.  I was pleasantly surprised by the ambience and d√©cor of the restaurant.  It felt like a cozy cabin like atmosphere outside the confines of your average LA restaurant.  The wait staff was extremely attentive and offered us water and to take our drink order right away.  The list of specialty cocktails looked interesting so we each tried one.  The drinks I would say were the only thing slightly disappointing and is my reason for the 4 stars instead of 5.  Maybe I picked the wrong drink, but it tasted like a watered down, bland version of what was described.  Fast forward to the food, we tried a little bit of everything throughout the menu and was so happy with every item we ordered.  Our server was very attentive and kept everything coming in a timely manner.  Even halfway through our meal, the manager came by to ask how everything was and was very friendly.  And to top it all off, we were there for about 2.5 hours without being rushed the least bit.  My friend and I were thrilled we took a chance after having our doubts, which is maybe what made the experience even better.  Just make sure you make a reservation and go in with an open mind.  I hope to go back very soon and that they can match my next experience with my first.<//text>

< review>
One of my favorites. Koo has everything you want from a good sushi place. Quality ingredients, flavor, service, and ambiance. We started off our meal with their signature Spoonfuls of Happiness. Each order comes with two spoons, which are filled with a bunch of different ingredients that explode in your mouth. My favorite was the Uni one with the Quail egg. Now I normally do not like Uni whatsoever, but this spoon was amazing. Smooth and creamy and rich. The spoons come along with a shot of Sake as you are supposed to sip the sake first (I'm assuming to clear your taste buds) and then have the spoon. They say "sake spoon sake spoon"! We also ordered the Omakase. The 10pc one and the 7pc one. The 7pc comes with the Spoonful of Happiness so the GF and I did not have to order two for both of us. The quality of the fish was of course A+. So fresh! It was as if they had a contracted fisherman who literally caught the fish and teleported it right to the cutting board. The meal from start to finish was amazing. I believe if you sit at the bar they make the Omakase for you one piece by one piece, but we didn't want to wait for the bar. Highly recommended!</review>

<name>Brokn Brokn</name><Rate>5<//Rate>< Text>
This is a great FamCamp  available in March Air Reserve Base in Moreno Valley CA. This a true no frills spot,  there is a grassy area with a few chairs for your pets to do their business. Laundry and showers available in the office. Mike the person that works the office is great.

It's right off of the 215 on Cactus Ave. once you enter the main gate go straight for about a mile and a 1/2 your going to go almost to the Air traffic control tower and the park will be on your left hand side.

The PX and Commissary are outside of base but just about a 5-7 drive from the famcamp. Walmart and assorted shopping is 10 minutes away a few exits up the 215.< /Text>
